So we concede that they are the pillars, but with the Lawgiver considering them as a single reality, and granting them unity, and this reality necessarily has its fruits attached to it, which is legal validity (sihha). So it is not correct that they are in themselves neither prescribed nor reprehensible, and reprehensibility only occurs when their fruits do not result, that is when a condition or pillar is missing. So the non-prescribed is something else, not they. In other words: the prohibited prayer: is it an individual of the prayer that the Lawgiver considered or not? On the second, then what came is the prohibition of prayer? Rather of something else, and the texts reject that. Similarly, what occurred from the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them all) of prohibiting a certain prayer invalidates it. On the first, it includes the pillars considered by the Lawgiver and the conditions considered for its existence, otherwise it would necessitate the existence of a thing without its pillar and condition, which is the clearest impossibility, not suitable as the object of prohibition. And if it is with conditions and pillars, it exists as the Lawgiver considered it, with rulings arranged, so it is not essentially invalid, nor itself evil. And since the Wise has prohibited, there must be some type of evil, and that is only due to an evil attribute or adjacency. To all this Imam Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) alluded in his refutation of the one who said that divorce during menstruation is not effective because it is prohibited: that if divorce during menstruation does not occur, then what thing is forbidden? And by what act did the divorcer disobey during menstruation? And there remains no prohibition of divorce. This speech has no dust on it at all, nor does it depend on validity being included in the concepts of legal acts. And it has been established that the void evil in itself is impossible, because validity is included in the concept of prayer and fasting and their likes. And the prayer and fasting that are prohibited in themselves are not prayer and fasting due to the absence of the essential, which is validity. So invalid prayer is impossible, so it cannot be the object of prohibition. So the legal act that is attached to prohibition is valid in itself, prohibited due to an attribute. This exposition shows signs of approval from Shaykh Ibn al-Humam and the author (Muslim al-Thubut) in the Principles (al-Usul). And it is not hidden from you that the claim that validity enters the essence of legal acts is a claim without evidence, and no trace of this appears in the books of the mashayikh. Rather, what appears from their expressions is that validity is among the necessary consequences, so by its absence the act ceases; and that is where the disagreement lies. So in clarifying this, one must return to what we have presented of the clear truth, so reflect, perhaps it benefits you in many places. And this, even if it leads to repetition and length, preserves you from error, as it is not devoid of benefit and achievement. No. ( The second required topic: on the branches from it: fasting on the day of Eid. For it is prescribed for us in its essence not its description. And what appears from examining their speech about it is that it is fasting that was prohibited, so it must be such that if one fasts on it, his fast occurs as fasting, and he sins; otherwise, the prohibition would not be against fasting but against something else. And if it occurs as fasting, it must include the pillars and conditions, so prescription is necessary; otherwise it would not be fasting nor the object of prohibition. This is the fullest exposition of their speech. And what was mentioned and established for the speech of Imam Hujjat al-Islam (al-Ghazali) is not a refutation of it—that then it would be missing a condition or pillar, so the prohibition does not attach to it—this is a mistake. And then there is discussion: that it has been narrated in some reports in the negative form, like: 'No, there is no fasting in these days.' So this implies that the reality of fasting is negated and it is not a prohibition such that possibility is required, so the truthfulness of the word 'fast' for the performed act is not necessary. And it has passed in the second chapter of the second article on the issue of the conjunction of obligation and prohibition what guides you to it. From the third article on the linguistic principles to its refutation, so remember. And it was objected to him that then it follows that wudu enters the concept of prayer, because prayer without purification is not prayer according to you, so it must be that part of it is missing, and it is nothing but wudu for example, so it follows that it enters while it is an external condition, this is a fallacy, as in the commentary on al-Mukhtasara, matching its text. Then this is a necessary consequence for them as well, for valid prayer is only what is concurrent with purification, so it would follow that it is included in it. So whatever your answer is, it is our answer. And it is answered by preventing the necessity, because the condition is only for the realization of the named according to the Law, not that it enters the reality of the named. It was said: If the named were an expression of the pillars themselves without considering an additional matter, it would be realized when the pillars are realized even if the condition is missing, and if the Lawgiver does not consider this existence, it would necessitate the annihilation of the existent, and its solution will come if Allah wills from us. And in the well-known view, it is established that the restriction to the concurrence of the condition is internal, not the condition itself. So prayer, for example, is an expression of the specific pillars concurrent with the conditions, and they (conditions) are external to them, as is the valid prayer according to you. It was said: What is meant by necessity (luzum) is that it necessarily becomes a part of the concept (mafhum) of prayer, not a part of its reality (haqiqa). And by 'part of the concept' they mean that understanding the concept of something depends on understanding it, so that it is part of its title. For the concept of sight is part of the concept of blindness, not part of the reality, so that its indication of it is by inclusion (tadamun). There is no doubt about this necessity, for if the pillars were not conceived as restricted by the concurrence of conditions, prayer would not be distinguished from what is not prayer, namely the pillars not concurrent with them. I say first: The dependency (tawaqquf), i.e., the dependency of conceiving prayer on wudu, for example, such that it enters its title, is prevented. Its verification is that prayer, for example, is an expression of these pillars, but not absolutely; rather, such that they become a manifestation (misdaq) of the glorification of Allah Almighty, and this glorification is like the form (sura) and species (naw'iyya) for the reality of prayer, while the pillars are like its matter (madda). So when the pillars exist and become a manifestation of glorification, the reality of prayer exists in reality like other realities. But the conditions are things on which the existence of this glorification depends. So by the absence of these conditions, what is like the form ceases, so the reality ceases. And this does not necessitate the dependency of its understanding on understanding the conditions nor their entry into the title, just as the life of an animal and the existence of its specific form depend on a specific temperament, but it does not require its entry into its reality nor into its concept. So what was said—that if the restriction were not internal, then prayer without wudu would be prayer, otherwise it would necessitate the annihilation of the existent—is repelled. For the dependency of understanding is established. And what we mentioned is hovered around by what is in the Hashiya: 'The revealers (mukashifun) of the realities of acts of worship and their forms distinguish between the valid accepted one and others without looking at the condition. They call the accepted ones 'spirits in the world of subtle realities.' And what is meant by 'revealers' are the noble mystics (sufis), for they say of the acts of worship that they have forms in the barzakh world, as attested by the texts of the weighing of deeds and the texts of the guarding of deeds, as is reported in the authentic hadith that Sura al-Mulk guards its reciter in the Hereafter, and the noble Qur'an intercedes, etc. And the relation of the valid act to the invalid one is like the relation of the living to the dead in our world. This is the most just evidence that prayer has an aspect like the soul for the body, and the conditions are only conditions for its existence. So understand. And I say secondly: If the necessity is conceded, then the invalidity of the necessary consequence is prevented, for it does not necessitate the absence of a difference between pillar and condition. The impossibility is only in the necessity of being a part, so reflect. The followers of the three Imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) said: First: The prohibition in shar'i matters...
Source pages p. 434

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on Muslim al-Thubut, expanding on the nature of validity (sihha) in acts of worship. The author begins by analyzing whether the prohibited prayer can be considered a valid instance of prayer. If it is not valid, then the prohibition would not be on prayer but on something else, which contradicts the texts. Therefore, the prohibited act must be valid in essence but prohibited due to an attribute. The author endorses Imam Muhammad's argument regarding divorce during menstruation: if it were not valid, there would be no prohibition and no sin. The author then clarifies that the preferred Hanafi view (as seen in the books of the mashayikh) is that validity is a necessary consequence (lazim) of the act, not part of its essence (haqiqa). This is applied to fasting on Eid: it is valid in essence (since it meets the pillars and conditions) but prohibited due to the day. The objection that this would make wudu part of the concept of prayer is addressed: wudu is a condition for the realization of the named (the reality of prayer), but not part of its concept or reality. The author uses the analogy of a living body: the soul (form) is the glorification of Allah, and the pillars are the matter. Conditions are like the specific temperament needed for life but not part of the essence. The mystics (sufis) also distinguish valid from invalid acts without considering conditions, comparing valid acts to living beings. Thus, the Hanafi position holds that prohibited acts can be valid in essence.

Key Terms
الصحة (al-sihha): Legal validity; in this passage, it is argued to be a necessary consequence of an act meeting its pillars and conditions, not part of its essence.
الحقيقة (al-haqiqa): The reality or essence of an act; here, the intrinsic nature of an act of worship, which is distinct from external conditions.
اللازم (al-lazim): A necessary consequence; here, validity follows necessarily from the existence of the act under proper conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view discussed, what is the status of a prayer performed without wudu?
A) It is a valid but sinful prayer.
B) It is not considered prayer at all because wudu is a condition for its existence.
C) It is a valid prayer because the pillars are present.
D) It is valid and acceptable because the intention is present.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, validity is a necessary consequence of the act's existence, not part of its essence; therefore, a prohibited act can be valid in itself.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
12 min
Prohibition by Attribute Does Not Invalidate Essence for Vows
Argues that acts prohibited by external attribute remain valid for nathr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that a prohibition due to an external attribute (al-qabh bil-ʿaraḍ) does not corrupt the essence of an act, and use this to determine the validity of a vow (nathr).

Core Idea
An act prohibited by an external attribute remains valid in essence for vowing.

A common misconception is that any prohibited act is evil in itself and therefore cannot be the object of a valid vow. In this passage, the author clarifies the Hanafi position: an act like fasting on Eid or prayer in prohibited times is not inherently evil; the evil lies in an accompanying attribute. Since the vow attaches to the essence, it is valid. We will unpack this principle, examine its proof, and see how it resolves objections from the hadith 'لا نذر في المعصية'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core principle
Read the opening lines: 'القبيح لا يكون قبيحاً لعينه بل بالعرض'. The author distinguishes between essential ugliness and accidental ugliness. This is the foundational distinction.
2
Apply the principle to examples
The author gives three examples: fasting on Eid, prayer in prohibited times, and invalid sales. For each, identify the essence (e.g., fasting) and the external attribute (e.g., turning away from Allah's hospitality).
3
Address the hadith objection
The objection cites 'لا نذر في المعصية'. How does the author restrict 'disobedience' to essential evil? Trace the argument: the vow attaches to the essence, not the attribute. The attribute is what makes the act prohibited, but it is not part of the vowed act.
4
Understand the sharʿī reality (al-ḥaqīqah al-sharʿiyyah)
The author explains that when an act fulfills its pillars and conditions, the sharʿī reality is realized and its effects follow. The external attribute does not negate this reality; it only adds a separate ruling (e.g., the obligation to break the fast and make up).
5
Differentiate the Hanafi position from potential alternatives
Consider how a Shafiʿī might read the hadith as general. The Hanafi response shows that the word 'maʿṣiyah' in the hadith is interpreted narrowly—only acts evil in themselves, not those evil by attribute. This preserves the validity of vows for many acts that are otherwise permissible in essence.

(الإيجاب الذي هو النذر لكونه لا خبث فيه، وإنما هو في الوصف ولم يتعلق به النذر ، ثم إنه بعد النذر يؤمر بالإفطار وقضاء يوم مكانه، وكذا الصلاة في الأوقات المنهية، فإنه لا قبح فيها من حيث هي صلاة، إنما القبح لوقوعها في وقت تعبد فيه الشمس والشيطان، فيصح النذر بها أيضاً لعدم تعلقه بالتشبيه بعبادة الشيطان، وكذا الربا وسائر البيوع الفاسدة فإنها ليست خبيثة من حيث إنها مبادلة المال بالمال بالتراضي، وإنما قبل القبض لئلا يلزم تقرير الفساد الذي كان واجب الرفع من قبل الشارع، إذ لو ثبت الملك حل له المطالبة وهذا هو الفرق بين الصحيح والفاسد في ثبوت الملك قبل القبض وبعده فتدبر واعترض بأن غاية ما لزم أنه يصدق مسمى الصوم والصلاة والبيع على صوم العيد والصلاة وقت الاستواء والبيوع الفاسدة، لكن من أين لزم ثبوت استحقاق المحمدة للآتي بهما، وثبوت الملك في البيع الفاسد وهذا الاعتراض في غاية السخافة، فإنك قد علمت سابقاً أن الحقيقة الشرعية هي التي اعتبرها الشارع وهي المستجمعة للأركان والشروط ومتى تحققت هذه الحقيقة ترتب عليها الأحكام والثمرات الموضوعة تلك الحقيقة لأجلها، وإلا فلا فائدة في اعتبار حقيقة لا يترتب عليها ثمرة أصلاً، وقد مر من قبل، وجه لمنع ترتب الثمرات بعد تحقق أسبابها مع الشروط والأركان فتدبر فيه، ثم ربما يستشكل بأن انعقاد النذر بهذا الصيام أو الصلاة لا يصح، لأن المسلم روى أنه عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام قال : «لا نذر في المعصية ولا شك أن المعصية عامة، سواء كانت لذاته أو من قبل الوصف، فيلزم أن لا يصح النذر بها لكونها معصية قطعاً، وما يقال: إن الأداء لوجوب القضاء لأجل مصلحة فيه ولا معصية وانعقاد النذر أيضاً لهذه الفائدة ليس بشيء، لأن وجوب القضاء فرع وجوب الأصل، وإذ لم يعقل وجوب الأصل لكونه معصية لا نذر بها فلا قضاء وجوابه : أنا قد بينا أن صوم يوم العيد ليس معصية في حد نفسه، والنذر إنما تعلق به وإنما المعصية الإعراض المذكور ولم يتعلق به النذر، ولا نسلم أن المعصية عامة فيما يكون هو معصية أو مجاوره، كيف وإلا لم يصح النذر بالصلاة في الدار المغصوبة أو الوضوء على قارعة الطريق بل المراد بالمعصية ما تصدق عليه المعصية حقيقة، وحينئذ لا حاجة ما أجيب به باختيار رواية الحسن عن الإمام أبي حنيفة رضي الله عنه أنه إن أضاف النذر لصوم الغد يلزم الصوم وإن كان الغد يوم العيد، لأن ما نذر به ليس معصية، وإنما اتفق أن يكون عيداً، بخلاف ما إذا أضاف لصوم العيد فإنه معصية، مع أنه إن كانت المعصية لكون متعلق النذر مقارناً بالإعراض عن الضيافة فصوم العيد والغد كلاهما سواء، وإن كانت لتعلق النذر بما هو معصية، فليس في الصورتين المنذور معصية فتدبر وأنصف
The ugly is not ugly in its essence but accidentally. If the corruption of the description does not necessitate corruption of the essence, then fasting on the day of Nahr remains legislated; rather the corruption is due to the description of it being a turning away from the hospitality of Allah. So a vow to fast on the day of Eid is valid because it accepts the obligation which is the vow, since there is no evil in it; the evil is only in the description, and the vow is not attached to it. Then, after the vow, he is commanded to break the fast and make up a day in its place. Similarly, prayer in the prohibited times: there is no ugliness in it qua prayer; the ugliness is due to its occurrence at a time when the sun and the devil are worshipped. So a vow to pray at such times is also valid because it is not attached to imitating the worship of the devil. Likewise, usury and all invalid sales: they are not evil insofar as they are an exchange of property for property by mutual consent; the evil is only due to the condition of an increase or other corrupting conditions. The cause of establishing ownership is from the aspect of their being sales and exchange, but these contracts are obligatory to revoke and annul in order to avoid the corruption that comes from the description. Hence ownership is not established before possession, lest the corruption that the Lawgiver required to be removed be affirmed; because if ownership were established, he would have the right to demand it. This is the difference between valid and invalid in establishing ownership before and after possession, so ponder. An objection: The utmost that follows is that the name of fasting, prayer, and sale applies to fasting on Eid, prayer at midday, and invalid sales; but from where does it follow that the one who performs them deserves praise and that ownership is established in an invalid sale? This objection is extremely foolish. You have already learned that the shar'i reality is that which the Lawgiver considers, and it is that which comprises the pillars and conditions. When this reality is realized, the rulings and fruits placed for that reality follow; otherwise there is no benefit in considering a reality that yields no fruit at all. This has preceded. A point preventing the derivation of fruits after the realization of their causes with conditions and pillars, so ponder it. Then an objection might arise: The conclusion of a vow for such fasting or prayer is invalid because Muslim narrated that he (peace and blessings be upon him and his family and companions) said: "No vow in disobedience." There is no doubt that disobedience is general, whether it is in itself or due to a description. It follows that the vow is invalid because it is definitely disobedience. And what is said—that performance necessitates the obligation of making up due to a benefit in it and no disobedience, and that the conclusion of the vow is also for this benefit—is nothing, because the obligation of making up is a branch of the obligation of the original act. Since the obligation of the original act is not understood because it is disobedience, there is no vow for it, so no making up. The answer: We have shown that fasting on Eid is not disobedience in itself; the vow is attached to it; rather the disobedience is the mentioned turning away, and the vow is not attached to it. We do not accept that disobedience is general to what is itself disobedience or its attendant. How so? Otherwise a vow to pray in a usurped house or to perform wudu on a public path would not be valid. Rather, by disobedience is meant that which is truly called disobedience. Therefore, there is no need for what was answered by choosing the narration of Hasan from Imam Abu Hanifa (may Allah be pleased with him) that if he attaches the vow to fasting tomorrow, the fast is obligatory even if tomorrow is Eid, because what he vowed is not disobedience, it just happens to be Eid—unlike the case where he attaches the vow to fasting on Eid, for that is disobedience. But if the disobedience is due to the object of the vow being accompanied by turning away from hospitality, then fasting on Eid and tomorrow are both the same; and if it is due to the vow being attached to what is itself disobedience, then in both scenarios the vowed act is not disobedience. So ponder and be fair.
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the principle that prohibitions due to an external attribute do not corrupt the essence of an act. The author argues that acts like fasting on Eid, prayer in prohibited times, and invalid sales are not evil in themselves; the evil lies in an accompanying attribute (e.g., turning away from Allah's hospitality, imitating sun-worship, or illegal conditions). Therefore, a vow (nathr) to perform such acts is valid because the vow attaches to the essence, not the corrupting attribute. The passage then addresses two objections: (1) that even if the name applies, no good or ownership results; the author counters by explaining the shar'i reality—a reality consisting of valid pillars and conditions yields its proper legal effects. (2) The hadith "no vow in disobedience" is cited; the author clarifies that the act in itself is not disobedience; the disobedience is in the external attribute, so the vow is valid. The author also discusses a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa through Hasan ibn Ziyad, distinguishing between vowing to fast on Eid day versus the day after Eid, concluding that the vow is for the essence, not the attribute.

Key Terms
حقيقة شرعية (al-haqīqah al-sharʿiyyah): The reality defined by the Lawgiver, comprising pillars and conditions, that yields its intended rulings and effects.
نذر (nadhr): A vow to perform an act of worship; its validity depends on the act's essence being permissible.
معصية (maʿṣiyah): Disobedience to Allah; here defined as acts evil in themselves, not those evil by an external attribute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a vow to fast on Eid day considered valid according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because fasting on Eid is not prohibited at all.
B) Because the prohibition is due to an external attribute (turning away from Allah's hospitality), not the essence of fasting.
C) Because the hadith 'no vow in disobedience' is not authentic.
D) Because the vow overrides the prohibition.

Key Takeaway
A prohibition due to an external attribute does not invalidate the essence of an act for the purpose of a vow; only essential disobedience invalidates.

Hanafi Classification of Prohibition Due to Description (Nahy 'ala Wasf): Lazim vs Mujawir
Examining Hanafi division of prohibition into lazim and mujawir and their rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a prohibition attached to a description as lazim or mujawir and determine whether it invalidates the act according to Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Prohibition due to an inseparable description invalidates the act; a separable description makes it makruh tahrimi but not invalid.

This passage explores a key Hanafi usul principle: how does a prohibition that is attached not to the act itself but to a description of the act affect its validity? The Hanafi school draws a critical distinction between inseparable (lazim) and separable (mujawir) descriptions, leading to different rulings for acts like fasting on 'Eid and selling during the Friday adhan. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying the maxim that not every prohibition entails invalidity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the attached prohibition
Locate in the passage the examples where a prohibition is attached to a description, not the act itself: fasting on 'Eid, selling during adhan, marriage of tahlil, prayer in a usurped place.
These examples illustrate the general category of nahy 'ala wasf.
2
Classify the description as lazim or mujawir
For each example, determine whether the prohibited description (e.g., turning away from hospitality, neglecting Friday, intending tahlil, usurpation) is inseparable from the act or separable. Note the Hanafi criteria.
Lazim: fasting on 'Eid – the turning away is unavoidable. Mujawir: selling during adhan – can be done while still attending Friday.
3
Determine the hukm based on the classification and proof strength
Apply the Hanafi rule: if lazim and proven by a definitive (qat'i) proof, it is haram and invalid; if zanni, it is makruh tahrimi but not invalid. If mujawir, it is always makruh tahrimi and not invalid.
The passage states that lazim with qat'i proof is called haram; otherwise makruh. Mujawir is always called makruh (tahrimi).
4
Trace the practical consequence (thamarah): qada' for fasting on 'Eid
The passage discusses why Hanafis do not require qada' for a fast started on 'Eid and broken: the start is invalid, so there is no obligation to complete. Contrast with prayer in a disliked time where completion is required.
This illustrates the thamarah al-khilaf between Hanafi and Shafi'i.

ههنا شيء هو أنه لا يمكن الامتثال إلا باستصحاب المعصية حينئذ، ولا يليق بشأن الحكيم إيجاب مثل هذا الأمر، لكن الأمر غير خفي على المكشوف بحقيقة الأمر، فإن الحكيم ما أمر بهذا الفعل بالذات، بل إنما أمر بشيء يمكن مفارقته عن الوصف المنهي، والتقصير من المكلف يلزم اجتماعه مع الوصف المنهي، كما أنه أوجب إيفاء المنذور وليس من لوازمه الإعراض عن الضيافة المنهي، لكن لما نذر الصوم في العيد لزم من إيفائه الارتكاب ولا شناعة في إيجاب الحكيم مثل هذا فتدبر، ثم لما كان في الإيفاء ارتكاب محرم وفي الاجتناب عنه ترك واجب لكن إلى خلف والفوات إلى خلف ليس فواتاً بكل وجه اختير الحكم بالإفطار وإيجاب القضاء فافهم، وإنما أطنبنا الكلام ليكون الناظر على بصيرة ولا يزيغه ما تذهب إليه الأوهام في بادىء الرأي من استبعاد إيجاب شيء وتحريمه عن سواء السبيل.
Our scholars divided the factor (ghayr) by which evil occurs in the prohibited thing into two: inseparable (lazim), as in fasting on the day of 'Eid, for the prohibition is due to turning away from accepting hospitality, and the fast of the day of 'Eid is not free from it, although fasting in general is free from it; and into a neighboring matter (amr mujawir) that may be free from it, such as selling at the time of the call to prayer, for it is only prohibited due to neglecting the Friday prayer, and it may be free from it as in selling while walking to the prayer, and the marriage of a muhallil, for it is only prohibited due to its association with the intention of making permissible, and marriage may be free from it. So the first category, if established by a definitive proof, they call it haram; otherwise, makruh. And for the second category, they do not use the word haram; they only use the word makruh and say: selling at the time of call, prayer in a usurped house, and marriage of a muhallil are makruh, meaning makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). Then, they do not require qada' (making up) for one who begins fasting on 'Eid and then breaks it, because the obligation of qada' is only due to the obligation of completion, and the obligation of completion is due to the validity of starting and preserving what was performed, but the start is not valid, and what was performed is required to be lifted, so there is no preservation, so no obligation, so no qada'. However, they required completion of prayer when started in the disliked time, and they distinguished by saying that the time of fasting is measured (mi'yar), so its corruption affects the corruption of the fast from the beginning, and every part of it contains disobedience, which is turning away; unlike prayer, for its time is not measured, and not every part contains disobedience, and it is only completed with the sajdah. And you are not unaware that there is no role of being measured here, for both starts are equal in being disobedience due to the other. If this is the last of his argument about its causality for the obligation of completion, they are equal; otherwise, it is obligatory. So the better approach is to be content with the hadith of accompanying disobedience and say: The completion of the fast is only obligatory to preserve what was performed, and everything performed is not free from turning away; while the completion of prayer is only obligatory to preserve the tahrimah (opening takbir) from invalidation, and there is in the tahrimah no imitation of the worship of disbelievers, so no disobedience, so it does not exit from causality; disobedience is only in the performance of a pillar like standing, bowing, etc. Based on this, it is not objected that only a complete rak'ah would be prohibited, not less than that, because less than a rak'ah is not prayer [according to some views]; but less than a rak'ah is still a prayer act, so it is prohibited in these times like the rak'ah due to the existence of the prohibited imitation. Followers of Imam Malik said: The scholars deduced the prohibition of fasting on 'Eid from the prohibition reported about it, and there is no denial, so it is consensus. It was refuted first: that the prohibition is more general than your claim, so from its establishment its establishment does not follow. If what is meant by prohibition is prohibition for itself, then it entails invalidity; we deny the consensus, because the discussion is about invalidity due to description. Understand. Second: it is a description of the inseparable type, so from invalidity in it, invalidity does not follow in the separable case. So the proof does not apply to your claim. It may be answered that the deduction is only due to the prohibition, so there is no difference between inseparable and separable, but this is denied. So clarification is needed. Understand. Third: it is objected by prayer in a usurped place and similar, for its validity is agreed upon, even though the prohibition is attached to it due to the description [of usurpation]. Consider. It was answered with two aspects: first, that the prohibition is not attached to the prayer itself; only usurpation is prohibited, but the one praying performed it concurrent with usurpation, as zakat is not sin even if given to an undeserving person. Its answer: There are authentic reports about the prohibition of using another's property without permission, and this is from the necessities of religion. There is no doubt that performing it necessitates the effect of the prohibition, because prayer on usurped land is using it, so it becomes the object of prohibition, for general is like specific in effecting the ruling. Understand. Second: that the meaning is that the requirement of prohibition is that, and there is no impossibility of it being prevented by a hindrance, and here a hindrance prevented. Its answer: This is not sufficient; rather, the hindrance must be specified, because the prohibition, which according to you necessitates invalidity of the original, is present, so it does not change from its requirement without a specific repeller. Understand. Imam al-Shafi'i said in his deduction: The prohibition due to its description opposes the obligation of its original, so they do not combine, thus it necessitates invalidity. It was objected by karaha (disliked ruling) [that also indicates invalidity because rulings are all opposing]. So karaha of the description opposes the obligation of the original. The solution is that there is no opposition when the locus differs. So it was answered prima facie that it is apparently indicating non-obligation, meaning that the prohibition of a thing due to its description apparently indicates the non-obligation of the original due to the predominance of harm. (Like in al-Mukhtasar.) I say: This appearance is denied; rather, the apparent meaning is that the negation refers to the qualification. This is supported by what is related from 'Abd al-Qahir that the focus of the information is the qualification, both negatively and affirmatively. It is said: The purpose of Imam al-Shafi'i is that the prohibition of an object described by a description opposes the obligation of the described, and it is apparent in its non-obligation due to what was mentioned of the scholars' deduction. And what is from 'Abd al-Qahir means that the focus of the information is the qualification in this qualified thing, not the unqualified thing in other than that qualified thing. This is insufficient, for the opposition of the prohibition of an object described by a description, due to the description, to the obligation of the same object is denied, as in karaha; how [can it be] when there is no opposition when the object of attachment differs? And there is no discussion about the prohibition not due to the description. Similarly, its appearance in the non-obligation of the same object is denied. And the denial of the predecessors' deduction of prohibition on description for invalidity has passed. There remains something here: that it is not possible to comply except by accompanying disobedience at that time, and it is not befitting of the Wise to obligate such a matter. But the matter is not hidden from one who is disclosed the reality of the matter. For the Wise did not command this very act; rather, He commanded something that can be separated from the prohibited description, and the shortcoming of the obligated person causes its conjunction with the prohibited description. Just as He obligated fulfilling a vow, and it is not a necessary concomitant of it to turn away from the prohibited hospitality; but when one vowed fasting on 'Eid, fulfilling it necessitates committing the prohibited act, and there is no repugnance in the Wise obligating such. So reflect. Then, since fulfilling it involves committing a prohibited act, and avoiding it involves leaving an obligation, but leaving an obligation is loss, and loss is not loss in every respect, the ruling of breaking the fast and requiring qada' was chosen. Understand. And we have spoken at length so that the observer may be insightful and not be led astray by initial imaginings of improbability of obligating something and prohibiting it from the right path.
Source pages p. 438

Commentary
This passage discusses the important usul principle of how prohibition (nahy) affects the validity of acts when the prohibition is attached to a description (wasf) of the act rather than the act itself. The Hanafi scholars categorize the factor causing the prohibition into two: lazim (inseparable) and mujawir (separable). This distinction determines whether the act becomes invalid or merely disliked. For example, fasting on 'Eid is prohibited because it inevitably involves turning away from hospitality; this description is inseparable, so if proven by a definitive text, it is haram and invalid. However, selling during the Friday adhan is prohibited due to the description of neglecting the Friday prayer, which can be separated if one also goes to the prayer; thus it is only makruh tahrimi and not invalid. The passage then applies this to the issue of qada' for starting a forbidden fast: since the start is not valid, there is no obligation to complete it, so no qada'. This contrasts with prayer in a disliked time, where completion is required because the start is valid. The discussion includes the Maliki objection and the Hanafi response, as well as the Shafi'i view that prohibition due to description opposes obligation and necessitates invalidity. The teacher explains that the Shafi'i view is rebutted by the distinction of locus (mahall) and the fact that the description is not part of the act's essence. The conclusion is that prohibition due to description does not necessarily invalidate the act; the specific circumstances determine the ruling.

Key Terms
لازم (lazim): An inseparable attribute that causes prohibition and cannot be separated from the act.
مجاور (mujawir): A separable attribute that causes prohibition and can be avoided.
كراهة التحريم (karaha al-tahrim): A category of prohibition that is not haram but makruh tahrimi, meaning it is still sinful but not invalidating.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi classification in the passage, what is the ruling for a person who starts a fast on the day of 'Eid and then breaks it?
A) He must make qada' because the prohibition is haram.
B) He does not need to make qada' because the start was not valid.
C) He must complete the fast because the prohibition is only makruh.
D) He is not sinful because the prohibition is not on the fast itself.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a prohibition attached to a description only invalidates the act if the description is inseparable (lazim) and proven by a definitive proof; otherwise, the act remains valid but is makruh tahrimi.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
advanced
10 min
Effect of Ta'liq: Does a Condition Nullify the Legal Cause?
Determining whether a condition prevents cause or only effect in legal cause

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the effect of ta'liq on sababiyyah and explain why Ibn al-Hammam's critique shows that the dispute about mafhum al-shart is distinct.

Core Idea
A condition either nullifies the cause or only suspends the ruling — and this is not the same as linguistic implication.

In usul al-fiqh, when a legal cause is conditioned, does the condition destroy the cause itself or merely block its effect? The Hanafis and Shafi'is differ, and this dispute has been incorrectly linked to the issue of mafhum al-shart (implication of the condition). This lesson unpacks the precise points of contention, critiques a flawed derivation, and clarifies the correct relationship between these two discussions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
Determine the exact question: does the condition (ta'liq) prevent the cause from being a cause (sababiyyah) or only prevent the ruling from being established? The Hanafis hold the first, the Shafi'is the second.
Note that the cause here is the protasis (jaza') which is made a legal cause for the ruling.
2
Examine the attempted derivation
Qadi Imam Abu Zayd and Fakhr al-Islam built the issue of mafhum al-shart on this dispute. Understand why they thought the dispute over sababiyyah is relevant: if the condition nullifies the cause, then the absence of the ruling is due to absence of cause, not the condition; but if it only prevents the ruling, then the absence is due to the condition, leading to a linguistic implication.
Be careful: they are linking a legal dispute to a linguistic one.
3
Analyze Ibn al-Hammam's critique
Ibn al-Hammam argues that this derivation is an error. The 'cause' in the mafhum dispute is the word of the condition itself, while in this dispute it is the protasis as a legal cause. The two are conceptually different.
The correct distinction: mafhum al-shart is linguistic (does the condition imply negation?), while this dispute is legal (does the condition void causality?).
4
Distinguish the two issues
Understand that the nullification of causality only occurs in constructions made legal causes (insha'), while mafhum al-shart covers all conditional sentences, including reports. They cannot be directly derived from each other.
Even if causality is nullified, it does not automatically settle the linguistic question.
5
Apply the correct understanding
For the Shafi'is, the protasis indicates a general ruling and the condition specifies it like an exception. For the Hanafis, the protasis with the condition indicates only a restricted ruling. This difference leads to different treatments of conditional clauses in legal reasoning.
The Hanafi view: the protasis with condition is like a restricted statement; beyond it, the original principle (non-existence) holds.

مسألة التعليق هل يمنع السبب عن السببية أو الحكم عن الثبوت (فقط) لا السبب عن الانعقاد اختار الحنفية الأول والشافعية (الثاني) والقاضي الإمام أبو زيد والإمام فخر الإسلام بنيا عليه مسألة مفهوم الشرط، وقرر صاحب الكشف وغيره وجه الابتناء بأنه لما مال الشافعية إلى أن الجزاء سبب للحكم وموجب له والشرط يمنع ثبوت الحكم عند عدمه، فعدم الحكم لعدم الشرط عنده وعندنا لما منعه عن السببية وإيجاب الحكم عند عدمه فعدم الحكم لانتفاء السبب من ذلك؟ والموجب كما كان من قبل فليس لعدم الشرط دخل فيه بل هو عدم أصلي، قال الشيخ ابن الهمام هذا غلط، لأن السبب الذي يدعي الشافعية انتفاء الحكم بانتفائه في خلافية مفهوم الشرط هو مدلول لفظ الشرط، وفي هذه الخلافية المراد الجزاء الذي جعل سبباً شرعياً للحكم، هل تبطل سببيته بالتعليق أو لا، بل يمنع التعليق عن الحكم فقط، فأين هذا وهذا لا توجه له فإن الشيخين الإمامين لم يدعيا أن مراد الشافعية بالسبب الجزاء، بل مقصودهما أنه لما يمنع الشرط عن ترتب الحكم على السبب الذي هو الجزاء يكون انتفاء الحكم مضافاً إلى الشرط ، فصار مدلولاً له وليس فيه غلط في معنى السبب أصلاً، فالصواب ما ذكره مطلع الأسرار الإلهية في وجه التغليط أن مسألة مفهوم الشرط مسألة لغوية حاصلها، هل يدل الشرط لغة على انتفاء الحكم عند انتفائه أولا وهذه الخلافية شرعية، فإن الحاصل أن الذي جعل سبباً شرعاً هل تبطل سببيته شرعاً بالشرط والتعليق أم لا، فلا يصح تفرع الخلافية في مفهوم الشرط على هذه الخلافية ولك أن تقول : بطلان السببية أو المنع عن حكم السبب إنما يتأتى في الإنشاءات التي جعلت أسباباً شرعاً ومسألة مفهوم الشرط تعم كل تعليق خبراً كان أو إنشاء : فلا يصح التفرع ولك أن تقول أيضاً لو سلم بطلان السببية كما هو مزعوم الحنفية فلا يوجب نفي مفهوم الشرط، فإن النزاع باقٍ ،بعد فإنه وإن لم يكن الجزاء سبباً للحكم وأن ينتفي عند عدم الشرط لانتفاء السبب فهل يدل هذا التركيب لغة على الانتفاء أولا، وكذا لو سلم عدم بطلان السببية وانتفاء الحكم بمنع الشرط فلا يلزم أن الشرط دال لغة على انتفاء الحكم بل يجوز أن يكون انتفاء الحكم عند انتفاء الشرط أصلياً ويكون بقاؤه لوجود المانع ولا ينفع الذهاب إليه فتدبر، ثم لك أن تقول في تقرير الكلام إن الجزاء عند الشافعية مفيد للحكم على جميع التقادير لغة وموجب له، والشرط خصصه بتقدير وجوده وأخرج تقدير عدمه ولهذا عدوا الشرط من المخصصات فانتفاء الحكم عند عدم الشرط إنما جاء من تخصيص الشرط، فأفاد حكماً مخالفاً لغة كالاستثناء، إلا أنه مفيد للحكم المخالف في المنطوق والشرط في المسكوت، وأما عندنا فالجزاء مع الشرط يفيد حكماً مقيداً، وما وراءه يبقى على الأصل، سواء كان الحكم في الجزاء، والشرط قيد بمنزلة الظرف والحال، أو كان الحكم بين الشرط والجزاء فإنه إذا ألحق المغير أيّ مغير كان يبقى الكلام موقوفاً فعلى هذا بناء خلافية مفهوم الشرط على أن الشرط هل هو بمنزلة استثناء تقديرات ما وراءه عن الحكم الجزائي وكان الجزاء عاماً لها لغة وأن الشرط مع الجزاء مفيد لحكم مقيد فقط لا غير، فعلى الأول الشرط دال على نفي الحكم عما عداه لغة بخلاف الثاني بل حكم ما عداه مسكوت عنه، ولعل هذا هو مراد الإمامين ثم لما كان من جزئيات التركيبات الشرطية ما جزاؤه سبب شرعاً لحكم آخر، ولم تكن سببيته إلا لإفادة حكمه في محله، وكان الجزاء في نفسه مفيداً لحكم عام لغة أو عرفاً على رأيهم فهو تام في السببية والشرط إنما استثنى بعض التقادير فمنع تأثيره عليها، وأما عندنا فلما لم يفد إلا حكماً مقيداً لم تتحقق سببيته قرر الكلام في هذا المثال وعبر عن الشيء بملزومه، وفي كلام القاضي الإمام إشارة جلية إلى ما قلناه فإن عبارته الشريفة في،
Issue: The condition, does it prevent the cause from being a cause, or the ruling from being established (only), not the cause from being effective? The Hanafis chose the first, and the Shafi'is the second. Qadi Imam Abu Zayd and Imam Fakhr al-Islam built upon it the issue of the implication of the condition. The author of al-Kashf and others determined the aspect of derivation: because when the Shafi'is inclined to the view that the protasis is a cause for the ruling and necessitates it, and the condition prevents the establishment of the ruling when it is absent, then the absence of the ruling is due to the absence of the condition according to them. According to us, since it prevents it from being a cause and necessitating the ruling when it is absent, the absence of the ruling is due to the absence of the cause from that? And the necessary remains as before, so the absence of the condition has no role in it; rather it is original non-existence. Shaykh Ibn al-Hammam said: This is an error, because the cause that the Shafi'is claim the ruling is absent by its absence in the dispute about the implication of the condition is the meaning of the word of the condition, and in this dispute, what is meant is the protasis which has been made a legal cause for the ruling. Does its causality become void by the condition or not? Rather the condition prevents only the ruling. So where is this and that? It has no direction, for the two imams (Abu Zayd and Fakhr al-Islam) did not claim that the Shafi'is mean by the cause the protasis. Rather, their intention is that when the condition prevents the attachment of the ruling to the cause which is the protasis, then the absence of the ruling is attributed to the condition, so it becomes an implication of it. And there is no error in the meaning of the cause at all. So the correct is what the author of Matali' al-Asrar al-Ilahiyya mentioned regarding the aspect of the correction: that the issue of the implication of the condition is a linguistic issue, its substance being: does the condition linguistically indicate the negation of the ruling when it is absent or not? And this dispute is legal, for the substance is: does that which has been made a legal cause have its causality voided legally by the condition and suspension, or not? So it is not valid to derive the dispute about the implication of the condition from this dispute. And you may say: nullification of causality or prevention of the effect of the cause only occurs in constructions that have been made legal causes, while the issue of the implication of the condition encompasses every suspension, whether it be a report or a construction, so derivation is not valid. And you may also say: even if we accept the nullification of causality as the Hanafis claim, it does not necessitate negation of the implication of the condition, for the dispute remains; subsequently, even if the protasis is not a cause for the ruling and it is negated when the condition is absent due to absence of cause, does this construction linguistically indicate negation or not? Similarly, even if we accept that causality is not nullified and the ruling is absent due to prevention by the condition, it does not necessitate that the condition linguistically indicates the negation of the ruling; rather it is possible that the negation of the ruling upon the absence of the condition is original, and its remaining is due to the existence of a preventer, and resorting to that does not help. So reflect. Then you may say in explaining the statement: The protasis, according to the Shafi'is, indicates the ruling in all conditions linguistically and necessitates it, and the condition specifies it by the condition of its existence and excludes the condition of its non-existence, and for this reason they counted the condition among the specifiers. So the negation of the ruling when the condition is absent comes only from the specification of the condition, so it indicates a contrary ruling linguistically like exception, except that it indicates the contrary ruling in the expressed and the condition in the unspoken. According to us, the protasis with the condition indicates a restricted ruling, and what is beyond it remains upon the original, whether the ruling is in the protasis and the condition is a restriction like an adverb and circumstance, or the ruling is between the condition and the protasis; for if a modifier is appended, whatever modifier it is, the speech remains suspended. Upon this is built the dispute about the implication of the condition: whether the condition is like an exception of the estimations beyond it from the ruling of the protasis, and the protasis is general for them linguistically, and the condition with the protasis indicates only a restricted ruling, or not. According to the first, the condition indicates the negation of the ruling from what is other than it linguistically, contrary to the second; rather the ruling for what is other than it is passed over in silence. Perhaps this is the intention of the two imams. Then, since among the particulars of conditional constructions is that whose protasis is a legal cause for another ruling, and its causality is only to indicate its ruling in its place, and the protasis itself indicates a general ruling linguistically or customarily according to their view, then it is complete in causality, and the condition only excludes some estimations so it prevents its effect upon them. According to us, since it only indicates a restricted ruling, its causality is not realized. So the statement was decided in this example, and he expressed the thing by its concomitant. And in the statement of Qadi Imam there is a clear indication of what we said, for his noble phrase in, ...
Source pages p. 461

Commentary
This passage addresses a key usul issue: when a legal cause (sabab) is conditioned (ta'liq), does the condition nullify the cause entirely (sababiyyah) or only prevent the ruling (hukm) from being established? The Hanafis (including Abu Zayd and Fakhr al-Islam) hold that the condition prevents the cause from being a cause (first view), while the Shafi'is hold that the condition only prevents the ruling, leaving the cause intact (second view). The author explains that Abu Zayd and Fakhr al-Islam built the issue of mafhum al-shart (implication of a condition) on this dispute. However, Ibn al-Hammam critiques this derivation, arguing that the 'cause' in the mafhum dispute is the word of the condition itself, not the protasis as a legal cause. The correct view, according to the author of Matali' al-Asrar, is that the two issues are distinct: mafhum al-shart is a linguistic issue about whether the condition linguistically implies negation of the ruling, while the present dispute is a legal issue about whether the condition nullifies the legal causality. Therefore, the derivation is invalid. The author then provides a deeper analysis: for the Shafi'is, the protasis indicates a general ruling, and the condition acts like an exception, specifying the ruling to the case where the condition exists; thus, when the condition is absent, the opposite ruling is indicated linguistically. For the Hanafis, the protasis with the condition indicates only a restricted ruling, and what is beyond is left to the original principle (non-existence). The passage concludes by noting that in specific cases where the protasis is itself a legal cause for another ruling, the Shafi'i view may see the condition as excluding only some estimations, but the Hanafi view sees the protasis as not implying a general ruling, so causality is not realized. The author refers to the statement of Qadi Imam (likely Abu Zayd) as supporting his exposition.

Key Terms
التعليق (al-ta'liq): The attachment of a condition (shart) to a legal cause (sabab), suspending its effect.
السببية (al-sababiyyah): The property of being a legal cause that entails a ruling.
الجزاء (al-jaza'): The protasis or result clause in a conditional statement; in legal contexts, often considered the cause of the ruling.
مفهوم الشرط (mafhum al-shart): The implication of a condition: whether the condition linguistically indicates the negation of the ruling when the condition is absent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn al-Hammam, what is the main flaw in deriving mafhum al-shart from the dispute over ta'liq?
A) The Hanafis and Shafi'is actually agree on ta'liq, so there is no dispute.
B) The 'cause' in the two disputes is different: in ta'liq it is the legal cause, in mafhum it is the word of the condition.
C) The dispute about ta'liq is linguistic, not legal.
D) Mafhum al-shart is universally accepted regardless of the ta'liq dispute.

Key Takeaway
The dispute over ta'liq (whether a condition nullifies a legal cause) is a legal issue distinct from the linguistic issue of mafhum al-shart (whether a condition implies negation).

Pages p. 461 · Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
